  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_54c28d79-c9f1-4650-baec-29333ccd6e3d'
      });

<div id="review_3261141068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3261141068" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3261141068?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3261141068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10684116387606284814">Completely captivating!<br/><br/>New York author Stephen Tesher earned his MFA in playwriting from The New School, and his MA in Education from City College of New York. He writes plays (his plays have been produced in Toronto and New York), screenplays (FREEDOM MILE) and novels, BLACK ICE being his debut novel, followed by INTOLERANCE. His career has been as an educator –a 7th grade English teacher in Nyack, NY, a special education teacher with an emphasis on writing, and a coach. He writes about kids, l</span>
  <span id="freeText10684116387606284814" style="display:none">Completely captivating!<br /><br />New York author Stephen Tesher earned his MFA in playwriting from The New School, and his MA in Education from City College of New York. He writes plays (his plays have been produced in Toronto and New York), screenplays (FREEDOM MILE) and novels, BLACK ICE being his debut novel, followed by INTOLERANCE. His career has been as an educator –a 7th grade English teacher in Nyack, NY, a special education teacher with an emphasis on writing, and a coach. He writes about kids, learning, sports, and family. <br /><br />Drama is something Stephen Tesher writes well, and while not having seen his plays or his film, his ability to create a well paced and very visual ‘production’ in a novel is remarkable. The manner in which he opens this story is very much like a film clip – a terrifying incident of a brutal act, shared in an brief excerpt here ‘…At that moment I realized he would kill me next. If he could kill her, he could kill me without blinking. I needed to stop him! A tsunami of regret for everything wrong that I ever did to anyone and everyone in my life rose up along the turbulent shores f my conscience; it threatened to wipe it out…’ Tension created, and the story begins.<br /><br />The tenets of the novel focus on the coming of age of a young lad and includes so many of the obstacles that the period can confront – losing virginity, confronting the emptiness of life, encountering flaws in people that hamper love, and the dangerous escape routes of drugs and alcohol. <br /><br />Stephen Tesher condenses the challenges of youth in a superbly written story – ‘David Fischer is slipping. He’s a typical teenager from a dysfunctional home - divorced parents, annoying younger sister, girlfriend just dumped him - and he's hoping to meet the perfect girl. David's two best friends are not much help. One is rich, charming and a hit with the girls; the other is a drug dealer with an infatuation for the Israeli army. Consequently, David escapes into alcohol and drugs. Then David meets Kris, a mysterious, sexy older woman, and his world is changed... forever. But David discovers that the mysteries of Kris' life may be darker than he's ready for.’<br /><br />Out of this dramatic presentation of one teenager’s coming of age experience flows some sensitive insights into the crises youth’s encounter – and how they can be managed. This book is not only fine entertainment: it is also memorable food for thought. Very highly recommended. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10684116387606284814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2695234682" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2695234682" />
    <a title="Amina Ibrahim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84458901-amina-ibrahim"><img alt="Amina Ibrahim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545297088p2/84458901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2695234682?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amina Ibrahim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amina Ibrahim" href="/user/show/84458901-amina-ibrahim">Amina Ibrahim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84458901-amina-ibrahim?shelf=2019-ng-group-challenge">2019-ng-group-challenge</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2695234682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8791754864128292024">Black ice is like a void your heart. It won't go away and it will absorb everything else.<br/>This was a perfect book for me at a perfect time, a good change from all the fantasy books I've read recently. David Fischer is a seventeen-year-old teen with zero self confidence and the only virgin among his friends. When the new mystery girl, Kris acknowledges him, David feels on cloud nine. He ignores his friends advice and starts pursuing Kris knowing little of the danger he was going to fall in.<br/>The fir</span>
  <span id="freeText8791754864128292024" style="display:none">Black ice is like a void your heart. It won't go away and it will absorb everything else.<br />This was a perfect book for me at a perfect time, a good change from all the fantasy books I've read recently. David Fischer is a seventeen-year-old teen with zero self confidence and the only virgin among his friends. When the new mystery girl, Kris acknowledges him, David feels on cloud nine. He ignores his friends advice and starts pursuing Kris knowing little of the danger he was going to fall in.<br />The first page hooked me to the story. It's a snippet of what will happen three months later and I just had to read to find out what happens. At first, I didn't like David (Okay, for most of the book I didn't like him, but he redeemed himself by the end). He only thought of himself all the time. <br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Kris was raped and even then he was only thinking of himself, that's how bad he was  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It is difficult to say anything without further spoiling which I don't want to. But one thing I have to say, THE ENDING! It was soo good. After being frustrated half of the book, then curious the second half, the ending made me grin. I was so happy for David. I would have hugged him if he was in front of me. The whole book was filled with negativity, but the last chapter was just crammed with so much positivity; it made everything worth it.<br />I was provided with a copy of this book, through Reading Deals, and I gave an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_1870697230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1870697230" />
    <a title="Christine Somers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3523060-christine-somers"><img alt="Christine Somers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526245036p2/3523060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1870697230?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Somers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Somers" href="/user/show/3523060-christine-somers">Christine Somers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1870697230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1326480388823091417">When I started this book I believed it to be a young adult book but soon came to understand the language and situations are well beyond anything I would want a young person to read. But having said that, I found myself engaged in the story and finished the book in two days. The lead character David is consumed by and with girls, alcohol and drugs as is his two friend Zee and Lewis. <br/><br/>It is a coming of age story that requires David to confront the 'black empty' that consumes his life and in doing s</span>
  <span id="freeText1326480388823091417" style="display:none">When I started this book I believed it to be a young adult book but soon came to understand the language and situations are well beyond anything I would want a young person to read. But having said that, I found myself engaged in the story and finished the book in two days. The lead character David is consumed by and with girls, alcohol and drugs as is his two friend Zee and Lewis. <br /><br />It is a coming of age story that requires David to confront the 'black empty' that consumes his life and in doing so accept the flawed people he loves. Black Ice is also a thriller and a page turner. It is a good winter day read in front of a warm fire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1326480388823091417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1367970343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367970343" />
    <a title="K. M.  Baginski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33551523-k-m-baginski"><img alt="K. M.  Baginski" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        <a title="K. M.  Baginski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. M.  Baginski" href="/user/show/33551523-k-m-baginski">K. M.  Baginski</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367970343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8376751212191960598">Intimately relatable, David's conflicted conscience mirrors our human struggle to process childhood pain while maintaining core relationships. Tesher's vivid figurative imagery gives the story a pulse. Whether it was the mental cobwebs unconsciously feeding the black empty that is David's pain after his parent's divorce or, the giant crater left within him at the moment his father comes to visit as part of the custody agreement. The literary depth is unmistakable! Unforgettable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1380376917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1380376917" />
    <a title="Rebeca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25770490-rebeca"><img alt="Rebeca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442009446p2/25770490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1380376917?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebeca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebeca" href="/user/show/25770490-rebeca">Rebeca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25770490-rebeca?shelf=review-requested">review-requested</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380376917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6594761214318814795">I think this is officially the book rating I felt more conflicted about so far in my reading life.<br/><br/>On one hand I felt like some parts of the plot were a bit exaggerated and that there were fascinating characters and intereting situations that could've been explored further and weren't. A quick example: David falls for a mysterious girl, Kris, by the end of the book we discover why Kris is so mysterious but throughout the story the reader doesn't get the chance to feel as wrapped up in her "myster</span>
  <span id="freeText6594761214318814795" style="display:none">I think this is officially the book rating I felt more conflicted about so far in my reading life.<br /><br />On one hand I felt like some parts of the plot were a bit exaggerated and that there were fascinating characters and intereting situations that could've been explored further and weren't. A quick example: David falls for a mysterious girl, Kris, by the end of the book we discover why Kris is so mysterious but throughout the story the reader doesn't get the chance to feel as wrapped up in her "mysterish" aura as could be.<br /><br />On the other hand: Oh My Feels! Black Ice has one of the most perfect endings I've ever read! I won't give you a big and enthusiastic speech about it (even though I would love to) since this is a non-spoiler review but I'll tell you the following: at the start of this book I was stuck with the idea that this story was a good representation of how hard it can be to move on from you first love. I finished it realising not only that but also how important it is that you free yourself. If a person is keeps telling you how he/she wants you but also that they can't be with you right then, if you're stuck in a vicious cycle because you really like them and feel unable to move on, you have to realize that they will never let you go. They like having you there fully commited even thought they're not. You have to let go, you have to free yourself. And Black Ice presents the reader with an amazing prespective on this topic.<br /><br />I loved it I loved it I loved it. The only reason I won't give the fifth star really only has to do with a bit of character/situation exploration that lacked in my opinion and could've made this book a perfect read.<br /><br />Nevertheless it is still an amazing read and I strongly recommend it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6594761214318814795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dog Houses" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dog Houses" href="/user/show/113922974-dog-houses">Dog Houses</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3298622596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10058615777492658912">Focusing on the troubles of a teenage lad struggling under the shadow of a dysfunctional home and heartbreak, Black Ice is a coming-of-age thriller that hits you like a punch in the gut. Along with David, the reader is taken on a wild ride with intoxicating older woman Kris, who opens up his world to more than he could ever imagined, and plenty of danger too. Will the loveable David survive his affair with Kris? Or will he be dragged deep into troubles that he is not prepared for.<br/><br/>A great coming-</span>
  <span id="freeText10058615777492658912" style="display:none">Focusing on the troubles of a teenage lad struggling under the shadow of a dysfunctional home and heartbreak, Black Ice is a coming-of-age thriller that hits you like a punch in the gut. Along with David, the reader is taken on a wild ride with intoxicating older woman Kris, who opens up his world to more than he could ever imagined, and plenty of danger too. Will the loveable David survive his affair with Kris? Or will he be dragged deep into troubles that he is not prepared for.<br /><br />A great coming-of-age story that really gets into the mindset of a teenage boy that is looking for an escape from his life at home. Stephen Tesher has created an excellent and relatable protagonist in David, and it would be great to see him again in follow up novels in the future.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1405787952?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BookCupid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BookCupid" href="/user/show/5178308-bookcupid">BookCupid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5178308-bookcupid?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1405787952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16562639907725160344">Love can be as dangerous as black ice. One false illusion that everything is safe and <b>boom</b>, next thing you know, you can't even remember who you are anymore. <br/><br/>David lost his virginity to Kris, a loner who refuses to see him as anything other than a friend with benefits. He tries courting her with dates, including a weekend at a chalet, but Kris remains unmoved. So David turns to his pals, booze and drugs (just like after his parents divorce) and sets forward some crazy set of events. Can he rescu</span>
  <span id="freeText16562639907725160344" style="display:none">Love can be as dangerous as black ice. One false illusion that everything is safe and <b>boom</b>, next thing you know, you can't even remember who you are anymore. <br /><br />David lost his virginity to Kris, a loner who refuses to see him as anything other than a friend with benefits. He tries courting her with dates, including a weekend at a chalet, but Kris remains unmoved. So David turns to his pals, booze and drugs (just like after his parents divorce) and sets forward some crazy set of events. Can he rescue Kris from her haunting past? Is he willing to kill for her?<br /><br />Author Stephen Tesher twisted this new-adult contemporary novel into a thriller about a love gone wrong. Although, it was impossible to identify with David's rising anger or some turns of events, the dialogue kept the story flowing. It was realistic; harsh at times when David and his friends talked about girls. <br /><br />I'm glad the author ended the story with a lesson. Not all relationships can have fairy tale endings.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16562639907725160344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32897362-amanda?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32897362-amanda?shelf=books-for-boys">books-for-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2888020805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12876876243493038051">Overall, I liked this book. It had a number of common YA elements. I guess I was expecting to see David go into more of a downward spiral based on the description on the back of the book.<br/><br/>Yes, he was doing horrible things, he was going overboard with the drinking and drugs and blacking out, but I felt like we should have seen more instances that showed how much of a problem it was becoming for David. The biggest, most horrible thing was him walking out on Kris in the cabin, getting beaten up and </span>
  <span id="freeText12876876243493038051" style="display:none">Overall, I liked this book. It had a number of common YA elements. I guess I was expecting to see David go into more of a downward spiral based on the description on the back of the book.<br /><br />Yes, he was doing horrible things, he was going overboard with the drinking and drugs and blacking out, but I felt like we should have seen more instances that showed how much of a problem it was becoming for David. The biggest, most horrible thing was him walking out on Kris in the cabin, getting beaten up and having her get sexually assaulted (which I'm not denying was horrible, but there was no build up to this instance). It was like everything went from 0-60 real quick.<br /><br />Additionally, it was interesting to see the way David dealt with losing his virginity and how different it is for boys than girls, more often we hear/see it from a female's perspective and it is important to see it from both sides. The pressure that boys feel to lose it, even if they're not mentally or emotionally ready to be that intimate with someone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12876876243493038051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rgpucuy/vaFjUDLHyniNDRZbumazgyCX9abuVd3yFSATlaUTcI81KgOdkn7OhimjQqKQznrqv8HzU/U//f5zYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mTtxMEwfeO9J0D/9bX9zV8h07XYetnL0f2J3QebKoZrMpLpR0C/wZCkdn0Rpgdf5nI3H3tff7aJ5l2wrxsbH2w==')})
  }
//]]>

Initially, as Penelope grows into her own in the burgeoning early Women’s Suffrage Movement, Edgar exerts pressure, promising to use his power and access to help her advance. But can he be trusted, or are his words part of an elaborate mind game played between him and his wife?
